## Syntax analysis

• Syntax analysis – the second phase of compilation

◆ Input: a sequence of token provided by the Lexical Analysis

◆ Output: a parse tree or abstract syntax tree (AST)

• Syntax specification

• RE/FA is not powerful enough (e.g., anbn, where n>0)

• So Grammar is needed, especially for context-free grammar (CFG)

## • Grammar G: $G = \left( \mathsf { V } _ { \top } , \mathsf { V } _ { \top } , \mathsf { S } , \delta \right)$

◆ ${ \mathsf { V } } _ { \top } \colon$ terminal symbols[终结符] = tokens from Lexical Analysis, leaves of the parse tree

◆ $\mathsf { V } _ { \mathsf { N } } .$ non-terminal symbols[非终结符], internal nodes of the parse tree

? S: start symbol[开始符号]

◆ δ: set of productions[产生式]: LHS -> RHS

## Sentential form, Sentence, Language[句型&句子&语言]

• Example:

$\mathsf { G } [ \mathsf { A } ] \colon \mathsf { A } \to \mathsf { c } \mid \mathsf { A } \mathsf { b }$

• Derivation: from grammar to language[文法到语言]

$$
\boxed { \ A \Rightarrow \boxed { \mathsf { c } } }
$$

sentence

$$
\bullet \boldsymbol { \vert } \mathsf { A } \Rightarrow \mathsf { A } \mathsf { b } \Rightarrow \mathsf { c } \mathsf { b }
$$

$$
\bullet \bullet \bullet \bullet \bullet \bullet \bullet \bullet \bullet \bullet \bullet \bullet \bullet
$$

$$
\bullet \bullet \mathsf { I A } \Rightarrow \mathsf { A b } \Rightarrow \mathsf { A b b } \Rightarrow \mathsf { A b b b } \Rightarrow \mathsf { c b b b }
$$

$$
\bullet | \mathbb { A } \Rightarrow \mathbb { A } \mathbb { b } \Rightarrow \mathbb { A } \mathbb { b } \mathbb { b } \Rightarrow \mathbb { A } \mathbb { b } \mathbb { b } \mathbb { b } \Rightarrow \mathbb { c } \mathbb { b } \mathbb { b } \mathbb { b } \Rightarrow \mathbb { c } \mathbb { b } \mathbb { b } \mathbb { b } \mathbb { b }
$$

Sentential form

## Overall Concepts

## • Derivation

◆ The application of the productions (from LHS to RHS)

 starts from the start symbol S to the input string

## • Reduce

◆ The reserve of derivation (from RHS to LHS)

 starts from the input string to the start symbol S

## • Parse tree

◆ Graphical representation of Derivation/Reduce without the order of productions

## • Ambiguous grammar

◆ A sentence has more than one parse (leftmost or rightmost) trees

◆ Ambiguity can be resolved by defining precedence and associativity for the grammar

## Chomsky Grammar System[乔姆斯基文法体系]

• Chomsky established the formal language system in 1956. He divided grammar into four types: 0, 1, 2, 3.

• Like context-free grammar, they are composed of 4 components G=(VT , VN , S, δ), but with different restrictions on productions.

![](images/05f90dab99e33b42bab0a05edb4c8068e9bc6a3e48a48dd1d6b50223c712b02c.jpg)  
Noam Chomsky

◆ Type 0 — unrestricted grammar [0型文法,无限制文法]

◆ Type 1 — context sensitive grammar(CSG) [1型文法,上下文有关文法]

◆ Type 2 — context free grammar (CFG) [2型文法,上下文无关文法]

◆ Type 3 — regular grammar [3型文法,正则文法]

## Chomsky Grammar System[乔姆斯基文法体系]

<table><tr><td rowspan=1 colspan=1>Class</td><td rowspan=1 colspan=1>Grammar</td><td rowspan=1 colspan=1>Restriction</td><td rowspan=1 colspan=1>Recognizer</td></tr><tr><td rowspan=1 colspan=1>3</td><td rowspan=1 colspan=1>Regular</td><td rowspan=1 colspan=1>A →aB or A-→a,where $\mathsf { A } , \mathsf { B } \in \mathsf { N } \wedge \mathsf { a } \in \Sigma \cup \{ \mathsf { \varepsilon } \}$  $\mathsf { A } \to \varepsilon$ permitted if A is the start symbol and does not appear onthe right of any production.</td><td rowspan=1 colspan=1>Finite-StateAutomaton(FSA)</td></tr><tr><td rowspan=1 colspan=1>2</td><td rowspan=1 colspan=1>Context-Free</td><td rowspan=1 colspan=1> $\mathsf { A } \to \alpha ,$ where $\mathsf { A } \in \mathsf { N } \wedge \alpha \in ( \Sigma \cup \mathsf { N } ) ^ { * }$ </td><td rowspan=1 colspan=1>Push-DownAutomaton(PDA)</td></tr><tr><td rowspan=1 colspan=1>1</td><td rowspan=1 colspan=1>Context-Sensitive</td><td rowspan=1 colspan=1> $\alpha  \beta$ ，where $\alpha , \beta \in ( \Sigma \cup \mathsf { N } ) ^ { * } \land \alpha \neq \varepsilon \land | \alpha | \leq | \beta |$ β can&#x27;t be ε, unless α is the start symbol and does not appear onthe right of any production.</td><td rowspan=1 colspan=1>Linear-BoundedAutomaton(LBA)</td></tr><tr><td rowspan=1 colspan=1>0</td><td rowspan=1 colspan=1>Unrestricted</td><td rowspan=1 colspan=1> $\alpha  \beta ,$ where $\alpha , \beta \in ( \Sigma \cup \mathbb { N } ) ^ { * } \wedge \alpha \neq \mathfrak { E } .$ </td><td rowspan=1 colspan=1>Turing Machine(TM)</td></tr></table>

Source: Prof Wenjun Li @ SYSU

## Parse Tree VS Abstract Syntax Tree

• An abstract syntax tree (AST) is abbreviated representation[缩写表示] of a parse tree

• drops details without compromising meaning [在不影响意义的情况下删除推导细节].

![](images/475c9f1c475c717a449bfb3faab7b47eeea2a9c08fb80d3951b20c3052f80e82.jpg)  
Abstract Syntax Tree(AST)

## Parsers

## • Syntax analysis takes a sentence as the input, and outputs the parse tree or AST of the sentence

◆Top-down: from the root to the leaves, in each step:

 Which non-terminal to replace?

 Which production?

Bottom-up: from leaves to the root

 Shift or reduce?

 If reduce, then which production?

![](images/5ce63d1ec68a1ffd45e2b22ca323740f97363a513943aea91b20c1c33f3b028f.jpg)

## Top-down

![](images/cef1eb115231ea77c4c36587e3f330eb1ebe7eec9022a64f7b98513f00f3b565.jpg)

## Top-down Parsers

## • Top-down Parsing

Recursive-descent parsing [RDP, 递归下降语法分析]

• (immediate and indirect) left recursion -> remove left recursion

• Backtracking -> brutal force, not preferred due to complications and high overheads

. Predicative parsing – LL(k) [预测分析]

• Predict the right production based on the input symbol (i.e., lookahead), no backtracking!

• Preliminaries: (1) remove left recursion, (2) left factoring

• To enable prediction: FIRST and FOLLOW

$\mathsf { F I R S T } ( \alpha ) = \{ \textsf { a } | \alpha \Rightarrow \mathsf { a . . . , a } \in \mathsf { V } _ { \tau } \} ,$ ε can be included

• FOLLOW $( \mathbb { A } ) = \{ \textbf { a } | \textbf { S } \Rightarrow . . . , \mathbb { a } . . . , \mathbb { a } \in \mathbb { V } _ { \intercal } \} ,$ \$ can be included

• Prediction based on the input symbol a when expanding A:

• For A with $A \to \alpha \mid \beta$ , where FIRST(α) and FIRST(β) are disjoint, i.e., chose the one with a inside its FIRST set.

• If all FIRST sets do not contain a, but $\mathfrak { s } \in \mathsf { F l R S T } ( \mathfrak { a } )$ while $\mathsf { a } \in \mathsf { F O L L O W } ( \mathsf { A } )$ , chose FIRST(α)

## Remove Left Recursion[消除左递归]

• Immediate left recursion can be eliminated by the following technique, which works for any number of $\mathsf { A } \cdot$ productions.

◆First, group the productions as

$\mathsf { A } \to \mathsf { A } \alpha _ { 1 } \mid \mathsf { A } \alpha _ { 2 } \mid . . . \mid \mathsf { A } \alpha _ { \mathsf { m } } \mid \beta _ { 1 } \mid \beta _ { 2 } \dotsc \mid \beta _ { \mathsf { n } }$ where no $\beta _ { \mathrm { i } }$ begins with an A.

Then, replace the A-productions by

$$
{ \mathbb A } \to { \mathbb B } _ { 1 } { \mathbb A } ^ { \prime } \mid { \mathbb B } _ { 2 } { \mathbb A } ^ { \prime } \mid \dots \mid { \mathbb B } _ { n } { \mathbb A } ^ { \prime } { \mathbb A } { \mathbb N } { \mathbb D } \quad { \mathbb A } ^ { \prime } \to { \mathbb alpha } _ { 1 } { \mathbb A } ^ { \prime } \mid { \mathbb alpha } _ { 2 } { \mathbb A } ^ { \prime } \mid \dots \mid { \mathbb \alpha } _ { m } { \mathbb A } ^ { \prime } \mid \varepsilon
$$

• Exercise-Remove Immediate left recursion.

$$
\mathsf { G } _ { 1 } [ \mathsf { E } ] \colon \mathsf { E }  \mathsf { E } + \mathsf { T } | \bigm \rVert _ { \vphantom { \mathsf { G } _ { 1 } ^ { \mathsf { B } } } } ^ { \mathsf { B } } ;
$$

$$
\bullet \mathsf { G } _ { 2 } [ \mathsf { E } ] \colon \mathsf { E } \to \mathsf { T E } ^ { \prime } ; \mathsf { E } ^ { \prime } \to + \mathsf { T E } ^ { \prime } \enspace | \enspace \pmb { \varepsilon } ;
$$

$$
T  T ^ { * } F \ | | \overline { { \mathsf { F } } } | ; ^ { \mathsf { \beta } }
$$

F → (E) | i.

$$
\mathsf { T } \to \mathsf { F T ^ { \prime } } ; \mathsf { T ^ { \prime } } \to { ^ { * } \mathsf { F T ^ { \prime } } } \mid \mathfrak { E } ;
$$

$$
{ \mathsf { F } }  ( { \mathsf { E } } ) \mid { \mathsf { i } } .
$$

## Compute FIRST

• To compute FIRST(X) for all grammar symbol X, apply the following rules until no more terminals or ε can be added to any FIRST set:

◆Rule1: If ${ \sf X } \in { \sf V } _ { \sf T }$ , then $\mathsf { F l R S T } ( \mathsf { X } ) = \{ \mathsf { X } \}$ . [X是终结符]

◆Rule2: If ${ \tt X } \in { \tt V } _ { \tt N }$ and $\textsf { X } \to$ ε exists, then add ε to FIRST(X). [非终结符,空式]

◆Rule3: If ${ \tt X } \in { \tt V } _ { \tt N }$ and ${ \sf X }  { \sf Y } _ { 1 } { \sf Y } _ { 2 } { \sf Y } _ { 3 } . . . { \sf Y } _ { { \sf k } } ,$ then [非终结符,非空式]

 If for some ${ \mathsf { Y } } _ { \mathrm { i } }$ and a terminal a: ① ε ∈ all $\mathsf { o f } \mathsf { F l R S T } ( \mathsf { Y } _ { 1 } ) , . . . ,$ F $| { \mathsf { R S T } } ( { \mathsf { Y } } _ { \mathsf { i - 1 } } ) , { \mathsf { i . e . } }$ $\Upsilon _ { 1 } . . . \Upsilon _ { \mathrm { i } - 1 } \stackrel { * } { \Rightarrow } \varepsilon ; \bigtriangleup$ a ∈ FIRST(Y ) \ {ε}. Then, a ∈ FIRST(X).

 E.g.,

 Everything in FIRST(Y1) \ {ε} is surely in FIRST(X).

 If ${ \sf Y } _ { 1 }$ doesn’t derive ε, then we add nothing more.

 But if $\Upsilon _ { 1 } \stackrel { * } { \Rightarrow } \varepsilon ,$ then we add FIRST $( Y _ { 2 } )$ \ {ε} , and so on…

 Add ε to FIRST $( \mathsf { X } ) ,$ if ε is in FIRST(Yi) for all $\mathsf { i } = 1 , 2 , \ldots \mathsf { k } .$

## Compute FIRST

• Next, we can compute FIRST for any string $\alpha = \sf X _ { 1 } X _ { 2 } . . . X _ { n }$ [符号串]

◆Add all non-ε symbols of FIRST $( { \sf X } _ { 1 } )$ to FlRST(⍺).

◆Add non-ε symbols of FIRST $( X _ { \mathrm { i } } )$ , 2≤i≤n, to FIRST(α), if FIRST $( \mathsf { X } _ { 1 } ) _ { \ r { 1 } }$ , ..., FIRST $( X _ { \mathfrak { j } - 1 } )$ all contain ε. [前i-1个都包含空串]

◆Add ε to FIRST(⍺), if FIRST $( \mathsf { X } _ { 1 } )$ , ..., FIRST $( X _ { n } )$ all contain ε.

[First(α)集合的计算本质上就是看α能推导出什么， First(α)包括所有α能推导出的句子的首个字符 (必须是终结符或空串)]

[给定 $\mathsf { a } \to \mathsf { X } _ { 1 } \mathsf { X } _ { 2 } . . . \mathsf { X } _ { \mathsf { n } }$ ，First(α)的计算基于单个First(Xi) 的计算（方法见上页）

## Compute FIRST

• Example: G[E]: E → TE’ ; E’ → +TE’ | ε ; T → FT’ ; T’ → \*FT’ | ε ; F →

(E) | id , compute the FIRST set of each non-terminal.

◆ FIRST(E):{ (, id }

◆ FIRST(T):{ (, id }

◆ FIRST(E’):{ +, ε }

◆ FIRST(T’):{ \*, ε }

◆ FIRST(F):{ (, id }

(3) If FIRST(X ), ..., FIRST(X ) all contain ε, add ε to FIRST(⍺)

It is necessary to determine whether the FIRST set has changed after each rule application.

E → TE’ FIRST(T) add to FIRST(E), FIRST(T) doesn’t contain ε

E’ → +TE’ FIRST(+) add to FIRST(E’), FIRST(+) doesn’t contain ε

E’ → ε ε add to FIRST(E’)

T → FT’ FIRST(F) add to FIRST(T), FIRST(F) doesn’t contain ε

T’ → \*FT’ FIRST(\*) add to FIRST(T’), FIRST(\*) doesn’t contain ε

T’ → ε ε add to FIRST(T’)

F → (E) FIRST(‘(’) add to FIRST(F), FIRST(‘(’) doesn’t contain ε

F → id FIRST(id) add to FIRST(F)

## Compute FOLLOW

• To compute FOLLOW(A) for all non-terminals A, apply the following rules until nothing can be added to any FOLLOW set.

◆Rule1: Place \$ in FOLLOW(S), where S is the start symbol.

◆Rule2: If there is a production A → αBβ, then everything in FIRST(β) except ε is in FOLLOW(B).

◆Rule3: If there is a production A → αB, or a production A → αBβ, where FIRST(β) contains ε, then everything in FOLLOW(A) is in FOLLOW(B).

[FOLLOW(A)计算的本质是在看这个A后 (不包含A本身的推导结果) 的符号 (必须是终结符或结束符号)]

[给定A → αBβ, FOLLOW(B)计算基于FIRST(β)的计算

## Compute FOLLOW

• G[E]: E → TE’ ; E’ → +TE’ | ε ; T → FT’ ; T’ → \*FT’ | ε ; F → (E) | id

◆ FIRST(E):{ (, id };FIRST(T):{ (, id };FIRST(E’):{ +, ε };FIRST(T’):{ \*, ε };FIRST(F):{ (, id }.

◆ FOLLOW(E):{ \$, ) }

◆ FOLLOW(T):{ +, \$, ) }

◆ FOLLOW(E’):{ \$ , ) }

◆ FOLLOW(T’):{ +, \$, ) }

◆ FOLLOW(F):{ \*, +, \$, ) }

A → αBβ

(1) If A is the start symbol, \$ ∈ FOLLOW(A)

(2) Everything in FIRST(β) except ε is in FOLLOW(B).

(3) If β does not exist or FIRST(β) contains ε, then everything in FOLLOW(A) is in FOLLOW(B).

◆ Place \$ in FOLLOW(E), since E is the start symbol.

◆ E → TE’

 FIRST(E’) except ε is in FOLLOW(T).

 Everything in FOLLOW(E) is in FOLLOW(E’).

 Since FIRST(E’) contains ε, then everything in FOLLOW(E) is in FOLLOW(T).

◆ E’ → +TE’ | ε

 FIRST(E’) except ε is in FOLLOW(T).

 Everything in FOLLOW(E’) is in FOLLOW(E’).

 Since FIRST(E’) contains ε, then everything in FOLLOW(E’) is in FOLLOW(T).

## Non-recursive LL(1) Parser [非递归]

• Input buffer[输入串]: contains the string to be parsed, followed by the “end marker” \$.

• Stack[推导的中间结果]: holds a sequence of grammar symbols and the symbol \$ to mark the bottom of the stack. It may contain:

◆Terminals that have yet to matched against the input symbol.

◆Non-terminals that have yet to be expanded.

![](images/d3cfabf636542ce1f9012d563501e72b588ce97dfce365b5027ea05edce364a8.jpg)

Parsing Table M[A,a] [语法分析表]: an entry containing production “A→…” or error.

Predictive Parsing Program[语法分析程 序]: Execute the action according to <stack top, current input symbol> 159

## LL(1) Parse Table [预测分析表]

<table><tr><td rowspan=8 colspan=1>G[E]:E→TEE&#x27;→+TE&#x27;丨εT→FT&#x27;T&#x27;→ *FT&#x27;丨εF→(E)|id</td><td></td><td></td><td></td><td></td><td></td><td></td><td></td><td></td></tr><tr><td rowspan=2 colspan=1></td><td rowspan=2 colspan=1>id</td><td rowspan=2 colspan=1>+</td><td rowspan=2 colspan=1>*</td><td rowspan=2 colspan=1>（</td><td rowspan=2 colspan=1>）</td><td rowspan=2 colspan=1>$</td><td></td></tr><tr><td rowspan=6 colspan=1>?Input symbol,lists all possibleterminals and $</td></tr><tr><td rowspan=1 colspan=1>E</td><td rowspan=1 colspan=1>E→TE&#x27;</td><td rowspan=1 colspan=1></td><td rowspan=1 colspan=1></td><td rowspan=1 colspan=1>E→TE&#x27;</td><td rowspan=1 colspan=1></td><td rowspan=1 colspan=1></td></tr><tr><td rowspan=1 colspan=1>E</td><td rowspan=1 colspan=1></td><td rowspan=1 colspan=1>E&#x27;→+TE&#x27;</td><td rowspan=1 colspan=1></td><td rowspan=1 colspan=1></td><td rowspan=1 colspan=1>E→m</td><td rowspan=1 colspan=1>E→m</td></tr><tr><td rowspan=1 colspan=1>T</td><td rowspan=1 colspan=1>T→FT&#x27;</td><td rowspan=1 colspan=1></td><td rowspan=1 colspan=1></td><td rowspan=1 colspan=1>T→FT&#x27;</td><td rowspan=1 colspan=1></td><td rowspan=1 colspan=1></td></tr><tr><td rowspan=1 colspan=1>T</td><td rowspan=1 colspan=1></td><td rowspan=1 colspan=1>T→m</td><td rowspan=1 colspan=1>T&#x27;→ *FT&#x27;</td><td rowspan=1 colspan=1></td><td rowspan=1 colspan=1>T→m</td><td rowspan=1 colspan=1>T&#x27;→ε</td></tr><tr><td rowspan=1 colspan=1>F</td><td rowspan=1 colspan=1>F→id</td><td rowspan=1 colspan=1></td><td rowspan=1 colspan=1></td><td rowspan=1 colspan=1>F→(E)</td><td rowspan=1 colspan=1></td><td rowspan=1 colspan=1></td></tr></table>

“predicts” the correct action based on one lookahead

Reject on reaching error state

Accept on end of input & empty stack

FIRST(E):{ (, id } FOLLOW(E):{ \$, )}

FIRST(T):{ (, id } FOLLOW(T):{ +, \$, )}

FIRST(E’):{ +, ε } FOLLOW(E’):{ \$ , )}

FIRST(T’):{ \*, ε } FOLLOW(T’):{ +, \$, )}

FIRST(F):{ (, id }. FOLLOW(F):{ \*, +, \$, )}

## LL(1) Parsing Algorithm [非递归算法]

## • Algorithm Step-by-Step based on <X, a>:

◆X: symbol at the top of the stack

◆a: current input token

◆ If ${ \sf X } \in { \sf V } _ { \top } ,$ [栈顶符号为终结符] and

 X == a == \$, declare SUCCESS, stop parsing.

 X == a != \$, pop X from stack and move the current input symbol forward one.

 X != a, declare ERROR, input is rejected, stop parsing.

◆ If ${ \mathsf { X } } \in { \mathsf { V } } _ { \mathsf { N } } ,$ [栈顶符号为非终结符] and

 M[X, a] has a production about X, pop X and push right side of production to stack.

$\mathsf { M } [ \mathsf { X } , \mathsf { a } ] = = \mathsf { e m p t y } ,$ declare ERROR, input is rejected, stop parsing.

![](images/178893f9b96ca5e015592cc84b4c255308ee535ba5b566ce4649e62febc43216.jpg)

![](images/b15933b0db8c4afa0d30cccdb47a977c654fc8c345b71e1c994cf32522605179.jpg)

If M[X,a] = X → +TE’ Push to stack in Reverse Order [逆序入栈]

If M[X,a] = X → ε Only pop and push nothing

## Bottom-Up

![](images/576398986452c3ce45dd73c7da8601ff763681b1e4895b7f7348bbb87d0d3423.jpg)

## Bottom-up: Shift-Reduce [移入-归约]

• Shift-reduce parsing is a form of bottom-up parsing in which a stack[栈] holds grammar symbols and an input buffer holds the input string.

• Reduction[规约]: At each reduction step, a specific substring matching the body of a production is replaced[替换] by the nonterminal at the head of that production.

• Shift[移入]: During a left-to-right scan of the input string, the parser shifts zero or more input symbols onto the stack, until it is ready to reduce a string β of grammar symbols on top of the stack.

## Phrase and Handle

• G(E): E → T | E+T; T → F | T\*F; F → (E) | a | b | c

• For sentential form a \* b + c

• Phrase: a\*b+c, a\*b, a, b, c

• Simple Phrase: a, b, c

• Handle: a

短语：一个句型的语法树中任意树叶结点组成的短语

直接短语：只有父子两代的子树形成的短语

句柄：语法树中最左那棵只有父子两代的子树形成的短语

![](images/4a0a3126b13c1a2014c84f1a91548341acae8ad15aded559fb972be9534f953e.jpg)

## Viable Prefix [活前缀]

• A viable prefix[活前缀/可行前缀] is a prefix of a right-sentential form that does not pass the end of the rightmost handle of that sentential form.

◆Stack content is always a viable prefix, guaranteeing the shift / reduce is on the right track.

• Example 1: S ⇒ aEb ⇒ aaEb, the handle is aE, so the viable prefix is a,

aa, aaE, but not aaEb.

<table><tr><td rowspan=1 colspan=1>Stack</td><td rowspan=1 colspan=1>Input</td></tr><tr><td rowspan=1 colspan=1>$...</td><td rowspan=1 colspan=1>Handle...$</td></tr><tr><td rowspan=1 colspan=1>$..</td><td rowspan=1 colspan=1>andle...$</td></tr><tr><td rowspan=1 colspan=1>$...Ha</td><td rowspan=1 colspan=1>ndle...$</td></tr><tr><td rowspan=1 colspan=1>$...Han</td><td rowspan=1 colspan=1>dle...$</td></tr></table>

## LR(k) Parser

## • LR(k) : member of LR family of parsers

"L" stands for left-to-right scanning of the input.

"R" stands for constructing a rightmost derivation in reverse.

◆ "k" is the number of input symbols of the lookahead used to make number of parsing decision.

## • Comparison with LL(k) parser

◆ Efficient as LL(k): Linear in time and space to length of input (same as LL(k)).

◆ Convenient as LL(k): Can generate automatically from grammar – YACC, Bison.

More complex than LL(k): Harder to debug parser when grammar causes conflicting predictions.

More powerful than LL(k): Handles more grammars: no left recursion removal, left factoring needed.

## LR Parser

![](images/2374778bf084e4da95107f91d6d1aa3158d8b6737e37bbb1b31915899e537a8b.jpg)

• The stack holds a sequence of states, $S _ { 0 } S _ { 1 } . . . S _ { m }$

colspan=1>8</td></tr><tr><td rowspan=1 colspan=1>7</td><td rowspan=1 colspan=1>r1</td><td rowspan=1 colspan=1>r1</td><td rowspan=1 colspan=1>r1</td><td rowspan=1 colspan=1>r1</td><td rowspan=1 colspan=1>r1</td><td rowspan=1 colspan=1></td><td rowspan=1 colspan=1></td></tr><tr><td rowspan=1 colspan=1>8</td><td rowspan=1 colspan=1>r2</td><td rowspan=1 colspan=1>r2</td><td rowspan=1 colspan=1>r2</td><td rowspan=1 colspan=1>r2</td><td rowspan=1 colspan=1>r2</td><td rowspan=1 colspan=1></td><td rowspan=1 colspan=1></td></tr></table>

◆ States are to track where we are in a parse.

◆ Each grammar symbol $x _ { j }$ is associated with a state $\mathsf { \pmb { S } } _ { \mathrm { i } }$

• Contents of stack + input $( \mathsf { X } _ { 1 } \mathsf { X } _ { 2 } . . . \mathsf { X } _ { \mathsf { m } } \mathsf { a } _ { \mathsf { i } } . . . \mathsf { a } _ { \mathsf { n } } )$ is a right sentential form ◆ If the input string is a member of the language

• Uses $[ \mathsf { S } _ { \mathrm { i } } , \mathsf { a } _ { \mathrm { i } } ]$ to index into parsing table to determine action

## Possible Actions[可能的动作]

## • ACTION $[ \mathsf { S } _ { \mathsf { m } } ,$ ai] has four possible actions:

Shift $( \mathsf { s } _ { \mathsf { x } } )$ : the handle is not completed loaded in the stack

1. Shift the next input symbol onto the top of the stack

2. Add State x to the stack

• Reduce $( r _ { y } )$ : the handle is at the top of the stack

1. Pop the handle and all its associated states.

2. Reduce the handle by the $y ^ { \mathrm { t h } }$ production (say $\pmb { \Delta }  \mathsf { a l }$

3. Push A onto the stack

4. Push state $\mathsf { \pmb { S _ { j } } }$ by GOTO table, $\mathsf { S } _ { \mathrm { j } } = \mathsf { G O T O } [ \mathsf { S } _ { \mathrm { i } } , \mathsf { A } ]$ and $\pmb { S _ { \mathrm { i } } } \mathrm { i } s$ the current state.

## Accept

◆ $\mathsf { A C T I O N } [ \mathsf { S } _ { \mathrm { i } } , \mathsf { a } _ { \mathrm { i } } ] = \mathsf { A C C } ,$ then parsing is complete and successfully

## • Error

$\mathsf { A C T } | \mathsf { O N } [ \mathsf { S } _ { \mathrm { i } } , \mathsf { a } _ { \mathrm { i } } ] = < \mathsf { e m p t y } >$ , then report error and stop

## Construct Parse Table

• Construct parsing table:

• identify the possible states and arrange the transitions among them.

• Different Parsing tables

• LR(0) – Too weak (no lookahead)

• Simplest LR parsing, only considers stack to decide shift/reduce

• SLR(1) – Simple LR, 1 token lookahead

• lookahead from first/follow rules derived from LR(0)

• Keeps table as small as LR(0)

• LALR(1) – Most common, 1 token lookahead

colspan=1></td></tr><tr><td rowspan=1 colspan=1>4</td><td rowspan=1 colspan=1>r3</td><td rowspan=1 colspan=1>r3</td><td rowspan=1 colspan=1>r3</td><td rowspan=1 colspan=1>r3</td><td rowspan=1 colspan=1>s1</td><td rowspan=1 colspan=1>s2</td><td rowspan=1 colspan=1></td><td rowspan=1 colspan=1></td><td rowspan=1 colspan=1>7</td></tr><tr><td rowspan=1 colspan=1>6</td><td rowspan=1 colspan=1></td><td rowspan=1 colspan=1></td><td rowspan=1 colspan=1>s1</td><td rowspan=1 colspan=1>s2</td><td rowspan=1 colspan=1></td><td rowspan=1 colspan=1></td><td rowspan=1 colspan=1>8</td></tr><tr><td rowspan=1 colspan=1>7</td><td rowspan=1 colspan=1>r1</td><td rowspan=1 colspan=1>r1</td><td rowspan=1 colspan=1>r1</td><td rowspan=1 colspan=1>r1</td><td rowspan=1 colspan=1>r1</td><td rowspan=1 colspan=1></td><td rowspan=1 colspan=1></td></tr><tr><td rowspan=1 colspan=1>8</td><td rowspan=1 colspan=1>r2</td><td rowspan=1 colspan=1>r2</td><td rowspan=1 colspan=1>r2</td><td rowspan=1 colspan=1>r2</td><td rowspan=1 colspan=1>r2</td><td rowspan=1 colspan=1></td><td rowspan=1 colspan=1></td></tr></table>

• fancier lookahead analysis using the same LR(0) automaton as SLR(1)

• LR(1) – 1 token lookahead, complex algorithms and big tables

• LR(k) – k tokens lookahead, even bigger tables

## Item[项目]

• The parsing table is based on the notion of LR(0) items (simply called items here) which are grammar rules with a special dot added somewhere in the right-hand side.

• For example, the rule A → XYZ has the following four items:

$$
\bullet \mathbf { A }  \bullet \mathbf { X } \pmb { Y } \pmb { Z }
$$

$$
\bullet \mathsf { A }  \mathsf { X } \bullet \mathsf { Y } \mathsf { Z }
$$

$$
\bullet \mathtt { A } \to \mathsf { X Y } \bullet \mathsf { Z }
$$

$$
\bullet \mathsf { A } \Rightarrow \mathsf { X } \mathsf { Y } \mathsf { Z } \ ^ { \circ }
$$

• Rules of the form A → ε have only a single item A → •

## Construct the LR(0) Automaton

• Each FA state corresponding to a set of items

• How to construct a state? -- closure operation

◆Closure: the action of adding equivalent items to a set

◆Example: $\mathsf { S } ^ { \prime } \to \mathsf { \cdot S } \mathsf { S } \to \mathsf { \cdot B B } \mathsf { B } \to \mathsf { \cdot a B } \mathsf { B } \to \mathsf { \cdot b }$

• How to construct transition form one state to another? -- goto operation

◆ A transition on symbol X from state i to state j

![](images/369166af4eb3d7226e19ff67b6489d752476db72d205f900c2f56213e9dcae17.jpg)

$$
( 0 ) \ S ^ { \prime } \to \ S
$$

$$
( 1 ) \mathsf { S } \to \mathsf { B B }
$$

$$
( 2 ) \ B \to \mathsf { a B }
$$

$$
( 3 ) \ B  { \ b }
$$

## CLOSURE()[闭包]

• Closure of item sets: if I is a set of items for a grammar G, then CLOSURE(I) is the set of items constructed from I by the two rules:

1. Initially, add every item in I to CLOSURE(I)

2. For any item A → ⍺·Bβ in CLOSURE(I), if B → γ is a production, and B → ·γ is not already there , then add item B → ·γ to CLOSURE(I)

◆ Apply the above rules until no more new items can be added to CLOSURE(I)

![](images/d08708784e4b6bdf441d88b3aed998f2ee788278325b7402c1bac3e889b0bfb2.jpg)  
Note: the location of the point ·

## GOTO()[跳转]

GOTO(I, X): returns state (set of items) that can be reached by advancing I by X

、 I is a set of items and X is a grammar symbol

◆ Return the closure of the set of all items $[ \mathsf { A } \to \alpha \mathsf { X } \cdot \beta ]$ when $[ \mathsf { A } \to \alpha \cdot \mathsf { X } \beta ]$ is in I

◆ Used to define the transitions in the LR(0) automaton

 The states of the automaton correspond to sets of items, and GOTO(I, X) specifies the transition from the state for I under input X

$$
\begin{array} { l } { \mathsf { G r a m m a r } \mathrm { : } } \\ { \mathsf { S ^ { \prime } } \to \mathsf { S } } \\ { \mathsf { S } \to \mathsf { B B } } \\ { \mathsf { B } \to \mathsf { a B } } \\ { \mathsf { B } \to \mathsf { b } } \end{array}
$$

$$
\begin{array} { r l } & { \mathsf { I } _ { 0 } \cdot } \\ & { \mathsf { S } ^ { \prime }  \cdot \mathsf { S } } \\ & { \mathsf { S }  \cdot \mathsf { B B } } \\ & { \mathsf { B }  \cdot \mathsf { a B } } \\ & { \mathsf { B }  \cdot \mathsf { b } } \end{array}
$$

$$
\begin{array} { l } { \displaystyle \vert _ { 2 } \colon } \\ { \displaystyle \mathsf { S } \to \mathsf { B } \cdot \mathsf { B } } \\ { \displaystyle \mathsf { B } \to \mathsf { \cdot a B } } \\ { \displaystyle \mathsf { B } \to \mathsf { . b } } \end{array}
$$

CLOSURE(S → B·B)

$$
G O T O ( I _ { O } , B )
$$

## The example

[建立第一个项]

[通过跳转建立后续项]

$$
\begin{array} { l } { \mathsf { G r a m m a r } \mathrm { : } } \\ { \mathsf { S ^ { \prime } } \to \mathsf { S } } \\ { \mathsf { S } \to \mathsf { B B } } \\ { \mathsf { B } \to \mathsf { a B } } \\ { \mathsf { B } \to \mathsf { b } } \end{array}
$$

## Example (cont.)

Grammar

(0) ${ \mathsf S } ^ { \prime } \to { \mathsf S }$

(1) $S  { \mathsf { B B } }$

(2) $\textsf { B } \to \mathsf { a B }$

(3) $a > b$

![](images/91a39645cb03d40ce10af1221cfbea0ba8495b89f1c57284832e8850a452585e.jpg)

“state j” refers to the state of the set of items Ij

## Construct LR(0) States[构造LR(0)状态集]

• Create augmented grammar G’ for G: [增广文法]

◆ Given $G \colon S  \alpha \mid \beta$ , create G’: $S ^ { \prime } \to S , S \to \alpha \mid \beta$

◆ Creates a single rule S’ → S that when reduced, signals acceptance

• Create 1st state by performing a closure on initial item $S ^ { \prime } \to \cdot S$ [初始状态]

Closure({S’→ ·S}) = {S’→ ·S, S → ·α, S → ·β}

• Create additional states by performing a GOTO on each symbol [添加状态]

◆ Goto({S’→ ·S, S → ·α, S → ·β}, α) =Closure({S → α·}) = {S → α·}

• Repeatedly perform gotos until there are no more states to add [重复操作]

$$
\begin{array} { r } { \left[ \begin{array} { l } { \mathsf { G r a m m a r } } \\ { 5 \to \alpha } \\ { 5 \to \beta } \\ { 5 \to \beta } \end{array} \right] \quad \Longrightarrow { \left[ \begin{array} { l } { \mathsf { G r a m m a r } ^ { \prime } } \\ { 5 \to \beta } \\ { 5 \to \alpha } \\ { 5 \to \beta } \end{array} \right] } \quad \Longrightarrow { \left[ \begin{array} { l } { \mathsf { C l o S U R E } ( 5 ^ { \prime } \to \ S ) } \\ { 5 ^ { \prime } \to \ S } \\ { 5 \to \alpha } \\ { 5 \to \beta } \end{array} \right] } \quad \stackrel { \cong } { \underbrace { \mathbb { B } } } \quad \underbrace { \left[ \begin{array} { l } { \mathsf { G r a m S U R E } ( 5 \to \alpha \cdot ) } \\ { 5 \to \alpha \cdot } \\ { 5 \to \alpha } \\ { 5 \to \beta } \end{array} \right] } _ { \textstyle \in \ : \emptyset } \quad \stackrel { \cong } { \underbrace { \mathbb { B } } } \quad \left[ \begin{array} { l } { \mathsf { C l o S U R E } ( 5 \to \alpha \cdot ) } \\ { 5 \to \alpha \cdot } \\ { 5 \to \alpha \cdot } \end{array} \right] } \end{array}
$$

## LR(0) Conflicts

• LR(0) has a reduce-reduce conflict if：

◆ Any state has two reduce items:

$X  \beta$ · and $\Upsilon  \omega$

• LR(0) has a shift-reduce conflict if:

◆ Any state has a reduce item and a shift item:

$$
{ \big \mathsf { X } } \to { \mathsf { \beta } } \cdot
$$

$$
{ \begin{array} { r l r l r l } & { \to \emptyset \cdot \operatorname { a n d } \lor \to \emptyset \cdot \operatorname { t } } & & { \quad \mathbf { I _ { 0 } } \colon } \\ & { } & & { \quad \mathbf { E } ^ { \prime } \cdot \mathbf { \hat { \times } } \mathbf { \hat { \times } } } \\ & { [ \begin{array} { l } { { \mathrm { c r a m m a r } } \cdot \mathbf { \hat { \times } } } \\ { \mathbf { E } ^ { \prime } \cdot \mathbf { \hat { \times } } } \\ { \mathbf { E } \cdot \mathbf { \hat { \times } } } \end{array} ] } & & { \quad \mathbf { E } \to \mathbf { \hat { \times } } \mathbf { \hat { \times } } } & & { \quad \mathbf { I _ { 1 } } \colon } \\ & { \to [ \begin{array} { l l } { 1 } & { \Gamma \mid \mathbf { \Omega } \lor \mathbf { z } } \\ { \Gamma  \mathbf { \hat { \times } } } \end{array} ] } & & { \quad \mathbf { E } \to \mathbf { \hat { \times } } \mathbf { \hat { \times } } } & & { \quad \mathbf { \hat { \times } } \mathbf { \hat { \times } } } \\ & { \to \mathbf { \hat { \times } } \mathbf { \hat { \times } } } & & { \quad \mathbf { \Omega } \lor \to \mathbf { \hat { \times } } } & & { \quad \mathbf { V } \to \mathbf { i } \ \cdot \mathbf { \hat { \times } } } \\ & { } & & { \quad \mathbf { \Omega } \lor \to \mathbf { \hat { \times } } \mathbf { \hat { \times } } } & & { \quad \mathbf { \Omega } \lor \mathbf { \hat { \times } } \mathbf { \hat { \times } } } \\ & { } & & { \quad \mathbf { V } \to \mathbf { \hat { \times } } \mathbf { \hat { \times } } } & & { \quad \mathbf { V } \to \mathbf { \hat { \times } } \mathbf { \hat { \times } } } \end{array} }
$$

## SLR(1): Simple LR(1)

## • SLR(1): Simple LR(1) with one lookahead

◆ Same LR(0) configurating sets, table structure, and parser operation.

◆ Allow both shift and reduce items as well as multiple reduce items.

◆ Use one token of lookahead to help arbitrate among the conflicts\*

◆ Reduce only if the next input token is a member of the FOLLOW set of the

nonterminal being reduced to

◆ Follow(T) = { +, ), ], \$ } Follow(V) = { = }

$$
\mathsf { F O L L O W } ( \mathsf { A } ) = \{ \mathsf { a } \mid \mathsf { S } \Rightarrow . . . \mathsf { A a } . . . ,
$$

$$
\mathsf { I } _ { 0 } \colon
$$

 If input t in Follow(T), reduce to T

$$
\mathsf { E } ^ { \prime } \to \mathsf { \Omega } ^ { \bullet } \mathsf { E }
$$

$$
\mathsf { E } ^ { \prime } \to \mathsf { E }
$$

 If input t in Follow(V), reduce to V

$$
\mathsf { E } \to \mathsf { E } { + } \mathsf { T } \mid \mathsf { T } \mid \mathsf { V } { = } \mathsf { E }
$$

$$
\mathsf { I } _ { 1 } \colon
$$

$$
\mathsf { E } \to \mathsf { \cdot } \mathsf { T }
$$

$$
\mathsf { T } \to ( \mathsf { E } ) \mid \mathsf { i d } \mid \mathsf { i d } [ \mathsf { E } ]
$$

$$
\mathsf { E }  \cdot \mathsf { E } { + } \mathsf { T }
$$

$$
\mathsf E \to \cdot \mathsf V { = } \mathsf E
$$

$$
T  \mathrm { i d } \cdot
$$

$$
{ \sf T }  { \sf i d } \cdot [ { \sf E } ]
$$

$$
{ \sf T }  \cdot ( { \sf E } )
$$

$$
\mathsf { V } \to \mathsf { i d }
$$

$$
\intercal  \cdot \mathrm { i d }
$$

$$
\mathsf { V } \to \mathrm { i d } \mathsf { \Omega } ^ { \bullet }
$$

 Else, the input [ will shift

$$
{ \mathsf { T } }  \cdot { \mathsf { i d } } [ { \mathsf { E } } ]
$$

$$
\vee  \cdot \mathsf { i d }
$$

## SLR(1) Grammars[SLR(1)文法]

• A grammar is SLR(1) if the following two conditions hold for each configurating set:

1. For any item $\mathsf { A } \to \mathsf { u } \cdot \mathsf { x } \mathsf { v }$ in the set, with terminal $\mathsf { \pmb { X } } ,$ there is no complete item B → w· in that set with x in Follow(B)

 In the tables, this translates no shift-reduce conflict on any state

2. For any two complete items A → u· and $\mathsf { B } \to \mathsf { v } ^ { . }$ in the set, the follow sets must be disjoint, i.e., Follow(A) ∩ Follow(B) is empty

 This translates to no reduce-reduce conflict on any state

 If more than one nonterminal could be reduced from this set, it must be possible to uniquely determine which using only one token of lookahead

## LR(1) Parsing

• LR parsing adds the required extra info into the state

◆ By redefining items to include a terminal symbol as an added component [让项目中包含终结符]

• General form of LR(1) items: $\mathsf { A } { \to } \mathsf { X } _ { 1 } { \ldots } \mathsf { X } _ { \mathrm { i } } \circ \mathsf { X } _ { \mathrm { i } + 1 } { \ldots } \mathsf { X } _ { \mathrm { j } } , \mathsf { c }$

◆ We have states $\mathsf { X } _ { 1 } . . . \mathsf { X } _ { \mathrm { i } }$ on the stack

◆ suppose $x _ { i + 1 } \ldots x _ { j }$ are on the stack, we can perform reduction when:  the next input symbol is a  a is called the lookahead of the configuration

• The lookahead only works with completed items[完成项]

◆ $A { \mathrm { - } } { \mathrm { > } } \mathsf { X } _ { 1 } { \mathrm { . . . } } \mathsf { X } _ { \mathrm { j } } { \mathrm { ~ \circ , ~ } } { \mathsf { a } }$

only reduce when next symbol is a (a is either a terminal or \$)

◆ Multi lookahead symbols: $\mathsf { A } \to \mathsf { U } ^ { \circ } , \mathsf { a } / \mathsf { b } / \mathsf { c }$

## LR(1) Parsing(cont.)

## • When to reduce?

◆ LR(0): if the configuration set has a completed item (i.e., dot at the end)

◆ SLR(1): only if the next input token is in the Follow set

◆ LR(1): only if the next input token is exactly a (terminal or \$)

Trend: more and more precise

## • LR(1) items: LR(0) item + lookahead terminals

◆ In many cases, LR(1) differs only in their lookahead components

◆ The extra lookahead terminals allow to make parsing decisions beyond the SLR(1) capability, but with a big price [代价]

 More distinguished items and thus more sets

 Greatly increases Goto and Action table size

$$
\boxed { \begin{array} { c c } { { \mathsf { S ^ { \prime } } \to \cdots \mathsf { S } } } & { { \mathsf { S ^ { \prime } } \to \cdots \mathsf { S } , \mathsf { S } } } \\ { { \mathsf { L R } ( 0 ) } } & { { \mathsf { L R } ( 1 ) } } \end{array} }
$$

## LR(1) Construction

## • Configuration sets

◆Sets construction are essentially the same with SLR, but differing on Closure() and Goto()

 Because of the lookahead symbol

## • Closure()

◆Given each item $\left[ \mathsf { A } \to \mathsf { u } \cdot \mathsf { B v } , \right.$ a] in I, for each production rule B -> w in G’, add [B -> ·w, b] to I:

 b ∈ First(va) && [B -> ·w, b] is not in I

 v can be nullable

◆Lookahead is the First(va), which are the symbols that can follow B

$$
\begin{array} { r l r l r l r l } & { ( 0 ) } & { S ^ { \prime } \to S } & & { \mathsf { I } _ { 0 } ; } & & { \mathsf { I } _ { 0 } ; } \\ & { ( 1 ) } & { S \to \mathsf { X X } } & & { S ^ { \prime } \to S , 5 } & & { \longrightarrow \qquad \begin{array} { l } { \mathsf { S } ^ { \prime } \to S , \mathsf { S } } \\ { \mathsf { S } \to \mathsf { X X } , \mathsf { F i r s t } ( \mathsf { x } \xi ) } \end{array} } & & { \Longrightarrow \qquad \begin{array} { l } { \mathsf { S } ^ { \prime } \to \mathsf { S } , \mathsf { S } } \\ { \mathsf { S } \to \mathsf { X X } , \mathsf { F i r s t } ( \mathsf { x } \xi ) } \end{array} } & & { \longrightarrow \qquad \begin{array} { l } { \mathsf { S } ^ { \prime } \to \mathsf { X X } , \mathsf { S } } \\ { \mathsf { X } \to \mathsf { X X } , \mathsf { S } } \end{array} } \\ & { ( 3 ) } & { \mathsf { X } \to \mathsf { b } } & & { \mathsf { X } \to \mathsf { b } , \mathsf { F i r s t } ( \mathsf { X } \xi ) } & & { \mathsf { X } \to \mathsf { b } , \mathsf { a } / \mathsf { b } } \end{array}
$$

## LR(1) Construction (cont.)

## • Goto(I, X)

◆For item $[ \mathsf { A } \to \mathsf { U } \cdot \mathsf { X } \mathsf { v } ,$ a] in I, Goto(I, $\mathsf { X } ) = \mathbb { C } | _ { 0 \mathsf { S U r e } } \left( [ \mathsf { A } \to \mathsf { u } \mathsf { X } \cdot \mathsf { v } , \mathsf { a } ] \right)$

◆Basically the same Goto function as defined for $\mathsf { L R } ( 0 )$

 But have to propagate the lookahead[传递] when computing the transitions

## • Overall steps

◆Start from the initial set Closure $( [ 5 ^ { \prime }  \cdot 5 , \$ 5 ] )$

◆Construct configuration sets following Goto(I, X)

◆Repeat until no new sets can be added

$$
\begin{array} { l l l l l } { \displaystyle \vert _ { 0 } : } & & { } & { \displaystyle \vert _ { 2 } : } & { } & { \displaystyle 1 _ { 2 } : } \\ { \displaystyle \textrm { S } \to \cdot \chi \chi , \ \xi } & { } & { \displaystyle \textrm { X } \to \times \cdot \chi , \ \xi } \\ { \displaystyle \textrm { X } \to \cdot \mathsf { a X } , \ \mathsf { a } / \mathsf { b } } & { } & { \displaystyle \textrm { X } \to \cdot \mathsf { a X } , \ \mathsf { F i r s t } ( \varepsilon \xi ) } & { } & { \displaystyle \textrm { X } \to \cdot \mathsf { a X } , \ \xi } \\ { \displaystyle \mathsf { X } \to \cdot \mathsf { b } , \ \mathsf { a } / \mathsf { b } } & { } & { } & { \displaystyle \mathsf { X } \to \cdot \mathsf { b } , \ \mathsf { F i r s t } ( \varepsilon \xi ) } & { } & { \displaystyle \textrm { X } \to \cdot \mathsf { b } , \ \xi } \end{array}
$$

## LR(1) Parse Table[解析表]

## • Shift[移进]

◆ Same as LR(0) and SLR(1)

Don’t care the lookahead symbols

## • Reduce[归约]

◆ Don’t use Follow set (that’s SLR(1), too coarse-grain[粗粒度])

◆ Reduce only if input matches lookahead for item

## • ACTION and GOTO[表格]

◆ If [A -> ⍺·aβ, b] ∈ Si and goto(Si , a) = Sj, Action[i, a] = Sj

 Shift a and goto state j

 Same as SLR(1)

◆ If $[ \mathsf { A } \to \mathsf { \alpha } \cdot , \mathsf { a } ] \in \mathsf { S } _ { \mathrm { i } }$ and next input is a, Action[i, a] = rk

 Reduce using ${ \sf k } ^ { \sf t h }$ production $( \mathsf { A } \to \mathsf { \alpha } \mathsf { \alpha } )$ if input matches a

 For $S \mathsf { L R } ,$ reduced if the next input is in Follow(A)

## Example

(0) ${ \mathsf S } ^ { \prime } \to { \mathsf S }$

$$
( 1 ) { \mathsf { S } } \to { \mathsf { X } } { \mathsf { X } }
$$

(2) $X  \mathsf { a X }$

(3) $x  6$

$$
S ^ { \prime }  \cdot S , \$ 5
$$

$$
{ \mathsf S } \to \cdot \mathsf { X } \mathsf { X } , \mathsf { S }
$$

$$
\textsf { X } \to \cdot \mathsf { a X } , \mathsf { a } / \mathsf { b }
$$

$$
{ \sf X }  { \sf \cdot a } { \sf X } , { \sf a } / { \sf b }
$$

## LALR(1) Parser

## • What’s the drawbacks of LR(1)?

◆ With state splitting, the LR(1) parser can have many more states than SLR(1) or LR(0) parser

 One LR(0) item may split up to many LR(1) items

 As many as all possible lookaheads

 In theory can lead to an exponential increase in #states

## • LALR (lookahead LR) – compromise LR(1) and SLR(1)[折衷]

◆ Reduce the number of states in LR(1) parser by merging similar states

 Reduces the #states to the same as SLR(1), but still retains the power of LR(1) lookaheads

◆ Similar states: have same number of items, the core of each item is identical, and they differ only in their lookahead sets

## Example

![](images/74fbe81785d34c8e5f52ebce81fb5a2711679402964a3708b6d1539ed93c740a.jpg)

## State Merging[状态合并]

• Merge states with the same core

◆ Core: LR(1) items minus the lookahead (i.e., LR(0) items)

All items are identical except lookahead

$$
\mathsf { I } _ { 3 } \colon
$$

$$
\mathsf { I } _ { 6 } \mathsf { : }
$$

$$
\textsf { X } \to \mathsf { a } \cdot \textsf { X } , \mathsf { a } / \mathsf { b }

$$
x  \mathsf { a } \cdot \mathsf { X } , \mathsf { S }
$$

$$
\mathsf { I } _ { 3 6 } \mathsf { : \Omega }

\mathsf { X } \to . \mathsf { a x } , \mathsf { a } / \mathsf { b }

{ \tt X } \to . { \tt a X } , \$ \sum

LR(1)  
Grammar (0) S’ -> S (1) S -> XX (2) X -> aX (3) X -> b

States 3 and 6: State 36  
States 4 and 7: State 47  
States 8 and 9: State 89

## Merge Effects[合并效果]

## 1. Merging of states can introduce conflicts[引入归约-归约冲突]

◆ Can introduce reduce-reduce (r-r) conflicts

 LR was introduced to split the Follow set on reduce action

 Merging reverts the splitting

◆ Cannot introduce shift-reduce (s-r) conflicts

 i.e., a s-r conflict cannot exist in a merged set unless the conflict was already present in one of the original LR(1) sets

## 2. Detection of errors may be delayed[推迟错误识别]

On error, LALR parsers will not perform shifts beyond an LR parser, but may perform more reductions before finding error

## Exercise 2

• 正则表达式可以表达语言 $L = \{ x n y z n , 1 \leq n \leq 1 0 \}$ 吗?可以，任何有穷集都是正规集，都可以用正规表达式来描述

• 正则表达式可以表达语言 $L = \{ x ^ { n } y z ^ { n } , \mathrm { n } > 0 \}$ 吗?

• 不行， 该语言是无穷的，不能用正规式表达

• 确定有限自动机(DFA)中不存在ε弧，所以DFA无法识别空串ε吗?• 错，DFA可以识别空串，但当且仅当开始状态与终止状态

• 给定正则式 (a| b)\*，使用汤普森构造法（ Thompson‘s Construction ）构造的有限自动机拥有几个状态?

![](images/07329bf5ff42e7d17f2f3cbf2527f5973b43e4e71d34d0c2a423be2d5a9ce091.jpg)

## Exercise 2

• 对于一个无二义性文法G，它的一个句子的最左与最右推导产生的分析树一定是一样的吗?

• 对的，是这样的。语法树会隐去推导顺序

• 怎么样判断一个文法是否为LL(1)型文法?

• 对文法中的每个产生式 A → α | β:

FIRST(α) ∩ FIRST(β) = ∅.

• If β ⇒ ε, then FIRST(α) ∩ FOLLOW(A) = ∅.

• LL(1)语法分析表行数与列数分别由哪些因素确定?

• 行数是该文法的非终结符个数，列数为终结符个数+1（ 结束符号\$ ）

• 设句型aaAb 的最右推导为 S⇒aBb⇒ aaAb ，句柄为aA ，该句型的活前缀是?• a, aa, aaA

## Exercise 2

• 找出以下文法中的句型的所有短语，直接短语，句柄

• 文法: G(E): E → T | E+T; T → F | T\*F; F → (E) | a | b | c

• 句型: a \* b + c

• 第一步：画出语法树

• 第二步：找出语法树的叶子节点• a, \*, b, +, c

• 第三步：由叶子节点找出短语

• a, a\*b, b, c, a\*b+c (why not \*b, b+c, \*, +?)

• 第四步：从短语中找出直接短语• a, b, c

. 第五步：从直接短语中找出句柄
